{
  "content": "# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nServer-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative resource management system in Kubernetes that enables safe, concurrent ownership of fields across multiple controllers, tools, and operators. Unlike imperative updates, SSA tracks which client (field manager) owns each field and automatically resolves conflicts when multiple clients attempt to modify the same fields. This guide details the subsystem architecture, component responsibilities, request flow, conflict handling, and operational patterns.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries\n\n### Purpose\n\nServer-Side Apply solves the multi-actor field ownership problem: In Kubernetes, many clients (human operators, deployment controllers, admission webhooks, operators) need to concurrently modify resources. Without coordination, their changes collide and overwrite each other.\n\nSSA provides:\n\n1. **Field-level ownership tracking** via `managedFields` in resource metadata\n2. **Conflict detection** when clients try to modify fields owned by others\n3. **Declarative merging** of configurations from multiple managers\n4. **Dry-run support** to preview apply operations before committing\n5. **Force-apply capability** to override field ownership when necessary\n\nThe core philosophy: *Clients declare their desired state; the server merges multiple declarations into a unified object while preserving ownership boundaries.*\n\n### Boundaries and Scope\n\n**In Scope (SSA responsibility):**\n- Patch processing for `application/apply-patch+yaml` and `application/apply-patch+cbor` content types\n- Structured merge diff using fieldpath-based conflict detection\n- Managed fields entry creation and update (in `.metadata.managedFields`)\n- Field manager identity tracking and conflict attribution\n- Dry-run execution and validation\n\n**Out of Scope (other subsystems):**\n- Authorization (handled by admission plugins before SSA)\n- Resource validation (handled by schema validation and admission webhooks)\n- Create/read/update/delete operations via other patch types (JSON Patch, Merge Patch, Strategic Merge Patch)\n- Storage layer mechanics\n\n### Upstream and Downstream Dependencies\n\n**Upstream Dependencies:**\n- **Admission plugins**: Pre-apply authorization and mutation checks\n- **Request routing**: HTTP handler registration in API server\n- **Type system**: API group/version/kind definitions via `k8s.io/api`\n- **Serialization**: YAML and CBOR codecs for encoding patch data\n\n**Downstream Dependencies:**\n- **Storage layer**: Persists updated objects and managed fields entries\n- **Audit logging**: Records all apply operations\n- **Field manager storage**: Stores managed fields in etcd within resource metadata\n- **Client libraries**: Consume generated apply configurations (applyconfigurations)\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Key Components and Responsibility Division\n\n### 2.1 Client-Side: ApplyConfigurations Generation and Usage\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/`\n\nApplyConfigurations are generated, type-safe builders that clients use to construct apply patches without manual JSON/YAML marshaling.\n\n#### ApplyConfiguration Structure\n\nEach Kubernetes resource type (Pod, Deployment, ConfigMap, etc.) has a corresponding apply configuration struct. Example from `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/core/v1/configmap.go`:\n\n```\nConfigMapApplyConfiguration struct {\n  metav1.TypeMetaApplyConfiguration\n  *metav1.ObjectMetaApplyConfiguration\n  Immutable *bool\n  Data map[string]string\n  BinaryData map[string][]byte\n}\n```\n\nKey characteristics:\n- **All fields are pointers or maps** (no slices) to encode \"field not specified\" as nil\n- **Builder methods** return `*ConfigMapApplyConfiguration` for fluent chaining (e.g., `WithName()`, `WithLabels()`)\n- **Extract functions** recover previously-applied configurations from a resource's managed fields\n\n#### Generation Process\n\n**Tool:** `applyconfiguration-gen` at `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/main.go`\n\nThe generator:\n1. Parses Kubernetes API types (e.g., `corev1.ConfigMap`)\n2. Creates apply configuration structs (one per type, including nested types)\n3. Generates builder methods and extractor functions\n4. Produces a `utils.go` file mapping `GroupVersionKind` \u2192 apply configuration type via `ForKind()` function\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/utils.go` (1921 lines)\n- Contains `ForKind(kind schema.GroupVersionKind)` function (line 130)\n- Dispatches on GroupVersionKind to return the appropriate apply configuration instance\n- Covers all Kubernetes API types across all versions\n\n#### Client Usage Pattern\n\n```\n// Build apply configuration\ncfg := corev1.ConfigMap(\"my-config\", \"default\").\n  WithData(map[string]string{\"key\": \"value\"})\n\n// Serialize to YAML\nbytes, _ := yaml.Marshal(cfg)\n\n// Apply via kubectl or client-go\nkubectl apply -f - <<< \"$bytes\"\n```\n\n### 2.2 Server-Side: Patch Handling and Field Management\n\n#### 2.2.1 HTTP Patch Endpoint\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/installer.go` (lines 890\u2013921)\n\nThe PATCH endpoint is registered for all resources. Supported patch types (from line 895\u2013903):\n- `application/json-patch+json`\n- `application/merge-patch+json`\n- `application/strategic-merge-patch+json`\n- `application/apply-patch+yaml`\n- `application/apply-patch+cbor` (conditional on `CBORServingAndStorage` feature gate)\n\nHandler factory: `restfulPatchResource()` wraps the core handler `handlers.PatchResource()`.\n\n#### 2.2.2 Main Patch Handler\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go`\n\n**Entry point:** `PatchResource()` function (line 68)\n\nResponsibilities:\n1. **Content-Type negotiation** (line 78\u201389): Validates patch type is supported\n2. **Request parameter parsing** (line 118\u2013129): Decodes `PatchOptions` from query string\n3. **Timeout enforcement** (line 99): Enforces at most 34s timeout or user's timeout if lower\n4. **Admission setup** (line 131, 200): Wraps admission plugins with `ManagedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController`\n5. **Patcher construction** (line 216\u2013245): Creates `patcher` struct with mechanism selection\n6. **Delegation** (line 247): Calls `patchResource()` for actual patch logic\n\n**Type: `patcher`** (line 272\u2013310)\n\nThe `patcher` struct holds all context for a single patch operation:\n- Request metadata (name, namespace, resource, subresource)\n- Validation functions (admission, authorization)\n- Codec for marshaling/unmarshaling\n- `mechanism` interface (set at patchResource time) for patch-type-specific logic\n- `updatedObjectInfo` for applying patches via storage layer's `GuaranteedUpdate` pattern\n\n**Patch Mechanism Interface** (line 312\u2013315):\n\n```\ntype patchMechanism interface {\n  applyPatchToCurrentObject(ctx context.Context, currentObject runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error)\n  createNewObject(ctx context.Context) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\nThree implementations:\n\n**a) `jsonPatcher`** (line 317\u2013321, method at line 323)\n- Handles JSON Patch and Merge Patch\n- Uses field manager for managed fields tracking\n- Encodes current object, applies patch, decodes result\n\n**b) `smpPatcher`** (search in patch.go for \"type smpPatcher\")\n- Handles Strategic Merge Patch\n- Preserves list merge semantics from schema\n- Also integrates with field manager for ownership tracking\n\n**c) `applyPatcher`** (line 488\u2013538)\n- Handles Server-Side Apply (YAML and CBOR)\n- Core SSA logic in method `applyPatchToCurrentObject()` (line 500\u2013530)\n- Calls `fieldManager.Apply()` (line 514) to perform structured merge\n- Validates with strict field validation if requested (line 521\u2013527)\n\n**Apply Patch Selection** (line 672\u2013686):\n\n```go\ncase types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n  p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n  p.forceAllowCreate = true\ncase types.ApplyCBORPatchType:\n  if !utilfeature.DefaultFeatureGate.Enabled(features.CBORServingAndStorage) {\n    return nil, false, fmt.Errorf(\"%v: unimplemented patch type\", p.patchType)\n  }\n  p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, cbor.Unmarshal, cbor.Unmarshal)\n  p.forceAllowCreate = true\n```\n\n#### 2.2.3 Admission Integration\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/admission.go`\n\n**Type: `managedFieldsValidatingAdmissionController`** (line 42\u201348)\n\nThis wrapper validates that mutating admission plugins don't corrupt `managedFields`:\n\n1. **Before admission** (line 69): Snapshots `managedFields`\n2. **Calls wrapped admission** (line 70): Executes user's admission plugins\n3. **After admission** (line 73\u201380):\n   - If `managedFields` became invalid, reverts to snapshot\n   - Issues warning via `warning.AddWarning()` about mutating admission side effects\n\nThis prevents admission plugins from breaking field manager state tracking.\n\n#### 2.2.4 Field Manager and Structured Merge\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go`\n\n**Type: `FieldManager`** (line 32)\n\nA type alias for `internal.FieldManager`. Factories:\n\n- `NewDefaultFieldManager()` (line 36): For regular resources with schema\n- `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager()` (line 47): For CRDs with dynamic schema\n\nCore method: `Apply(obj, patch, fieldManager, force)`\n\nInternally delegates to `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/fieldmanager.go` where:\n\n1. **Decodes patch** into unstructured map\n2. **Computes field diff** using structured-merge-diff library\n3. **Checks for conflicts**: If this manager doesn't own a field and another manager does, raises `ConflictError`\n4. **Merges owned fields** from the patch into the current object\n5. **Updates managed fields entries** to record ownership\n\n**Conflict Detection** (location: `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/conflict.go`)\n\n**Function: `NewConflictError()`** (line 33\u201343)\n\nWhen the `Apply()` call encounters fields owned by other managers:\n\n```\nApply failed with 3 conflicts:\n  conflicts with \"controller-manager\" using apps/v1:\n    - .spec.replicas\n    - .spec.template.spec.containers[0].image\n  conflicts with \"webhook\" using apps/v1 at 2024-02-28T10:30:00Z:\n    - .spec.strategy.type\n```\n\nEach conflict includes:\n- **Manager identity**: Name, API version, operation type, timestamp\n- **Path**: JSONPath to conflicting field\n- **Cause type**: `CauseTypeFieldManagerConflict`\n\n#### 2.2.5 Noop Optimization\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/fieldmanager/equality.go`\n\n**Function: `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer()`**\n\nSSA updates `managedFields` with current timestamps whenever an apply occurs, even if no actual field values changed (noop apply). This unnecessarily bumps resource versions.\n\nThe transformer:\n1. Compares objects while **ignoring managed field timestamps**\n2. If they're equal, skips the storage write\n3. Controlled via `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES` environment variable\n\n**Benefit:** Reduces unnecessary storage traffic and watch events for idempotent apply operations.\n\n### 2.3 Managed Fields Storage Format\n\n**Location:** Stored in `.metadata.managedFields[]` array in each resource\n\n**Structure** (from `k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/apis/meta/v1.ManagedFieldsEntry`):\n\n```\n{\n  manager: \"kubectl\",\n  operation: \"Apply\",          // or \"Update\"\n  apiVersion: \"apps/v1\",\n  time: \"2024-02-28T10:30:00Z\",\n  fieldsType: \"FieldsV1\",\n  fieldsV1: {\n    f:metadata: {...},\n    f:spec: {\n      f:replicas: {},\n      f:template: {...}\n    }\n  }\n}\n```\n\n**fieldsV1**: A nested map structure encoding which fields this manager owns. An empty object `{}` indicates a leaf field is owned.\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: End-to-End Control and Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Apply Request Journey\n\n**Step 1: HTTP Request Reception**\n\n```\nPATCH /api/v1/namespaces/default/configmaps/my-config\nContent-Type: application/apply-patch+yaml\nfieldManager=kubectl\nforce=false\n\nmetadata:\n  labels:\n    app: myapp\ndata:\n  config.yaml: |\n    key: value\n```\n\n**Step 2: Patch Handler Dispatch** (in `handlers.PatchResource()`)\n\n1. Extract content-type, validate it's supported (line 78\u201389)\n2. Parse namespace/name (line 91\u201395)\n3. Decode `PatchOptions` from query (line 118\u2013129)\n4. Select serializer based on content-type (line 136\u2013171)\n5. Construct admission chain with field manager validation (line 200)\n6. Build `patcher` struct and select mechanism (line 216\u2013687)\n   - For apply patches, selects `applyPatcher`\n   - Sets `forceAllowCreate = true` to allow creating via apply\n\n**Step 3: Core Patch Application** (patchResource flow, line 653)\n\nThe `patcher.patchResource()` method:\n\n```go\nfunc (p *patcher) patchResource(ctx context.Context, scope *RequestScope) (runtime.Object, bool, error) {\n  p.namespace = request.NamespaceValue(ctx)\n\n  // Select mechanism based on patchType (line 655\u2013687)\n  switch p.patchType {\n  case types.ApplyYAMLPatchType:\n    p.mechanism = newApplyPatcher(p, scope.FieldManager, yaml.Unmarshal, yaml.UnmarshalStrict)\n    p.forceAllowCreate = true\n  }\n\n  // Use storage layer's GuaranteedUpdate for optimistic concurrency control\n  return p.restPatcher.Update(ctx, p.name, rest.DefaultUpdatedObjectInfo{\n    Preconditions: &p.options.ResourceVersion,\n    UpdateFunc: p.applyPatch,  // Line 581: called by GuaranteedUpdate in retry loop\n  }, ...)\n}\n```\n\n**Step 4: GuaranteedUpdate Retry Loop** (in storage layer, not shown but invoked)\n\nStorage's `GuaranteedUpdate()` pattern:\n\n1. **Read current object** from storage (with resourceVersion)\n2. **Call UpdateFunc** (here: `patcher.applyPatch`) with current object\n3. **Compare resourceVersion**: If changed since read, retry from step 1\n4. **Write updated object** with managed fields\n\n**Step 5: Patch Mechanism Application** (`applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject`, line 500)\n\n```go\nfunc (p *applyPatcher) applyPatchToCurrentObject(ctx context.Context, obj runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n  force := false\n  if p.options.Force != nil {\n    force = *p.options.Force  // Force-apply if requested\n  }\n\n  // Unmarshal YAML/CBOR patch into unstructured map\n  patchObj := &unstructured.Unstructured{Object: map[string]interface{}{}}\n  if err := p.unmarshalFn(p.patch, &patchObj.Object); err != nil {\n    return nil, errors.NewBadRequest(...)\n  }\n\n  // Call FieldManager.Apply() - the core SSA logic (line 514)\n  obj, err := p.fieldManager.Apply(obj, patchObj, p.options.FieldManager, force)\n  if err != nil {\n    return obj, err  // Returns conflict error if fields owned by others\n  }\n\n  // Validate strict field parsing (line 521\u2013527)\n  if p.validationDirective == metav1.FieldValidationStrict {\n    if err := p.unmarshalStrictFn(p.patch, &map[string]interface{}{}); err != nil {\n      return nil, errors.NewBadRequest(...)  // Fail on unknown fields\n    }\n  }\n\n  return obj, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Step 6: Field Manager Apply Logic** (internal to `fieldmanager.go`)\n\nThe `FieldManager.Apply()` method (deep in internal package):\n\n1. **Build field ownership map** from current object's `managedFields`\n2. **Parse patch** as unstructured map\n3. **For each field in patch**:\n   - Check if current manager owns it (in `managedFields`)\n   - If another manager owns it:\n     - If `force=false`: add to conflicts list\n     - If `force=true`: take ownership, record in managed fields\n   - If no one owns it or this manager owns it: merge field value\n4. **Compute structured diff** using `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff` to handle list merging\n5. **Create/update ManagedFieldsEntry** with new ownership for this manager\n6. **Return merged object** or conflict error\n\n**Step 7: Admission Validation** (via `applyAdmission`, line 631\u2013649)\n\nAfter patch application:\n\n```go\nfunc (p *patcher) applyAdmission(ctx context.Context, patchedObject runtime.Object, currentObject runtime.Object) (runtime.Object, error) {\n  // Determine operation: Create if no current object, else Update\n  if hasUID, _ := hasUID(currentObject); !hasUID {\n    operation = admission.Create\n  } else {\n    operation = admission.Update\n  }\n\n  // Call admission plugins with patchedObject as new state\n  if p.admissionCheck != nil && p.admissionCheck.Handles(operation) {\n    attributes := p.admissionAttributes(ctx, patchedObject, currentObject, operation, options)\n    return patchedObject, p.admissionCheck.Admit(ctx, attributes, p.objectInterfaces)\n  }\n  return patchedObject, nil\n}\n```\n\nAdmission plugins can **mutate** the patchedObject. If they modify `managedFields` invalidly, the wrapper from step 2 reverts those changes and issues a warning.\n\n**Step 8: Storage Write** (via GuaranteedUpdate)\n\nIf all validation/admission passes:\n- **Increment resourceVersion**\n- **Write object + managed fields** to etcd\n- **Return HTTP 200 OK** with updated object in response body\n\n### 3.2 Create-via-Apply Flow\n\nWhen the resource doesn't exist (`force=false` or `force=true`):\n\n```\n1. applyPatcher.createNewObject() calls patcher.New() to create empty object\n2. applyPatcher.applyPatchToCurrentObject() applies patch to empty object\n3. FieldManager.Apply() treats empty object as \"no current manager ownership\"\n4. All fields from patch become owned by applying manager\n5. applyAdmission() runs with operation=Create\n6. Storage layer writes new object to etcd\n7. Returns HTTP 201 Created\n```\n\nSpecial case: If patch includes a UID and object doesn't exist:\n- Error: \"uid mismatch: the provided object specified uid X, and no existing object was found\" (line 606)\n- Prevents accidental creation with wrong UID\n\n### 3.3 Conflict Resolution Scenarios\n\n**Scenario A: Non-conflicting fields**\n\n```\nManager A owns: .metadata.labels, .spec.replicas\nManager B owns: .spec.template.spec.containers[0].image\n\nWhen B applies a patch touching only .spec.template.spec.containers[0].image:\n\u2192 Success: B already owns it\n```\n\n**Scenario B: Conflicting fields without force**\n\n```\nManager A owns: .spec.replicas (current value: 3)\nManager B applies patch: {spec: {replicas: 5}}\n\nWhen B's apply encounters .spec.replicas:\n\u2192 Conflict error (409 Conflict) with details:\n   \"Apply failed with 1 conflict:\n    conflict with \"controller-manager\" using apps/v1:\n    - .spec.replicas\"\n```\n\n**Scenario C: Force-apply overrides ownership**\n\n```\nSame as Scenario B, but request includes: force=true\n\nWhen B's apply encounters .spec.replicas:\n\u2192 Success: B takes ownership\n\u2192 .metadata.managedFields updated to show B now owns .spec.replicas\n\u2192 Old entry for A is modified to no longer list .spec.replicas\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: Failure Modes and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Field Conflict (409 Conflict)\n\n**Symptom:** Apply request returns HTTP 409 with structured conflict information\n\n**Root cause:** Client tries to apply fields owned by another manager without `force=true`\n\n**Detection:** In `FieldManager.Apply()` during field ownership check\n\n**Recovery:**\n- Option 1: Use `force=true` to take ownership (dangerous if field affects other managers)\n- Option 2: Coordinate with other manager to release field ownership\n- Option 3: Edit resource directly to remove other manager's entry from managedFields\n\n**Example:**\n```bash\n# Triggers conflict\nkubectl apply -f deployment.yaml\n\n# Resolve by forcing (use carefully!)\nkubectl apply -f deployment.yaml --force-conflicts\n\n# Or check who owns conflicting field\nkubectl get deployment my-deployment -o json | jq '.metadata.managedFields'\n```\n\n#### Invalid Managed Fields After Admission (Warning)\n\n**Symptom:** HTTP 200 with warning header in response\n\n**Root cause:** Mutating admission controller corrupted `.metadata.managedFields`\n\n**Detection:** Wrapper in fieldmanager admission plugin (admission.go line 74\u201380)\n\n**Resolution:**\n- Server reverts managedFields to pre-admission state automatically\n- Admin must fix or disable the offending admission webhook\n- Indicates webhook is not SSA-aware\n\n#### Strict Field Validation Errors (400 Bad Request)\n\n**Symptom:** \"error strict decoding YAML: unknown field 'typo'\"\n\n**Root cause:** Patch YAML contains unknown fields (when `fieldValidation=Strict`)\n\n**When triggered:**\n- Query parameter: `fieldManager=kubectl&fieldValidation=Strict`\n- Unknown fields in patch YAML\n\n**Recovery:**\n```bash\n# Fix typo in patch, or relax validation\nkubectl apply -f patch.yaml --field-validation=warn  # Warn instead of fail\n```\n\n#### Noop Apply Resource Version Bump (Operational)\n\n**Symptom:** `kubectl apply` causes resourceVersion to increment even with no field changes\n\n**Root cause:** ManagedFields timestamps are always updated, triggering storage write\n\n**Mitigation:** Server can avoid this via `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES` environment variable (managed by field equality transformer)\n\n**Impact:**\n- Increased watch event traffic\n- Unnecessary etcd writes\n- Controller reconciliation triggered on no-op applies\n\n### 4.2 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Tradeoff 1: Field Granularity vs. Simplicity\n\n**Decision:** SSA owns fields at arbitrary path depth (e.g., `.spec.template.spec.containers[0].resources.limits.memory`)\n\n**Benefit:**\n- Multiple managers can own different subfields of same object\n- Precise conflict attribution\n\n**Cost:**\n- Complex managed fields structure (nested maps)\n- Higher memory footprint for large objects\n- Conflict errors can be granular but hard to understand\n\n**Alternative considered:** Ownership at resource level only\n- Simpler but two managers can't safely share editing responsibilities\n\n#### Tradeoff 2: Force-Apply Semantics\n\n**Decision:** `force=true` unilaterally takes ownership of conflicting fields\n\n**Benefit:**\n- Allows operators to override when necessary\n- Useful for migrations (e.g., moving management from webhook to controller)\n\n**Cost:**\n- Can silently break other managers if misused\n- No audit trail of why force was needed\n- Tempts users to use it instead of coordinating\n\n**Mitigation:** kubectl warns on force-apply; audit logs include force flag\n\n#### Tradeoff 3: CBOR Support Behind Feature Gate\n\n**Decision:** `application/apply-patch+cbor` only available with `CBORServingAndStorage` feature gate enabled\n\n**Benefit:**\n- More efficient encoding than YAML (binary, smaller size)\n- Reduces bandwidth for large apply patches\n- Can use CBOR's type system for stricter validation\n\n**Cost:**\n- Users must enable feature gate (affects whole cluster)\n- Requires new tooling (CBOR doesn't have universal CLI support like YAML)\n- Debugging harder (not human-readable)\n\n**Why not default:** Stability risk; CBOR parsing bugs affect all apply operations\n\n#### Tradeoff 4: Admission Plugin Side Effects\n\n**Decision:** Mutating admission can modify objects but must not break managedFields\n\n**Benefit:**\n- Allows webhooks to inject defaults, normalize values\n- Doesn't require webhook to understand SSA\n\n**Cost:**\n- If webhook corrupts managedFields, server silently reverts them (warning only)\n- Webhook may not realize its mutations were rejected\n- Operator must monitor warnings to detect bad webhooks\n\n**Justification:** Webhooks predate SSA; breaking them would be incompatible\n\n#### Tradeoff 5: Extract vs. Full Reapply\n\n**Decision:** Clients can extract previously-applied configuration via `ExtractConfigMapFrom(resource, fieldManager, subresource)`\n\n**Benefit:**\n- Enables extract-modify-apply workflow without storing manifest separately\n- Recover what a manager applied even if object has changed\n\n**Cost:**\n- Extract returns only fields *still owned* by manager (not historical)\n- If another manager took ownership, those fields are missing\n- Users must handle incomplete extract gracefully\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Admission Plugins\n\n**Location:** Hooked in `PatchResource()` at line 200\n\nAdmission plugins can:\n\n1. **Mutate** the patched object (e.g., inject sidecar containers)\n2. **Validate** the apply (e.g., enforce naming conventions)\n3. **Reject** the apply (e.g., policy violations)\n\n**Interface:** `admission.Interface` with `Admit(ctx, attributes, objectInterfaces) error`\n\n**SSA awareness:** Plugins should NOT modify `managedFields` directly. If they do, the wrapper will revert invalid changes.\n\n**Example use case:** A security admission webhook that injects image-pull-secrets on Pod apply.\n\n### 5.2 Field Validation Modes\n\n**Configurable per-request via query parameter:** `fieldValidation=Strict|Warn|Ignore`\n\n- **Strict:** Unknown fields cause HTTP 400 (line 523\u2013524)\n- **Warn:** Unknown fields cause warning header in HTTP 200 (line 526)\n- **Ignore:** Unknown fields silently ignored (default, line 164\u2013166)\n\n**Extension point:** Server-side generators can introduce new fields without breaking old clients using Warn mode.\n\n### 5.3 Type Converter Customization\n\n**Location:** `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/fieldmanager.go` line 36\u201342\n\n**Factory functions:**\n\n- `NewDefaultFieldManager()`: Uses runtime.Scheme to define types\n- `NewDefaultCRDFieldManager()`: For CRDs without pre-defined schema\n\n**Customization hook:** Replace `TypeConverter` argument\n\n**Used by:** CRD controller to handle dynamic CRD schemas\n\n```go\n// From installer.go when creating field managers for a resource:\ntypeConverter := applyconfigurations.NewTypeConverter(scope.Scheme)\nfieldManager, _ := managedfields.NewDefaultFieldManager(\n  typeConverter,\n  scope.ObjectConvertor,\n  scope.Defaulter,\n  scope.Creater,\n  scope.Kind,\n  scope.HubGroupVersion,\n  subresource,\n  resetFields,\n)\n```\n\n### 5.4 Reset Fields Support\n\n**Parameter:** `resetFields` map passed to field manager constructor\n\n**Purpose:** Fields that should be force-reset to defaults when no manager owns them\n\n**Use case:** `status.observedGeneration` should auto-reset when no controller manages it\n\n**Mechanism:** In structured merge, if all managers release a field, reset it to schema default\n\n### 5.5 Apply Configuration Extraction\n\n**Location:** Generated function `ExtractConfigMapFrom()` in apply config files (line 78 in configmap.go example)\n\n**Purpose:** Recover a manager's previously-applied configuration from resource managedFields\n\n**Interface:**\n```go\nExtractConfigMapFrom(\n  configMap *corev1.ConfigMap,\n  fieldManager string,\n  subresource string,  // \"\" for main resource, \"status\" for subresource\n) (*ConfigMapApplyConfiguration, error)\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Custom extractors for non-standard resources\n\n**Example use:**\n```go\n// What did kubectl apply last time?\ncfg, err := corev1.ExtractConfigMap(pod, \"kubectl\")\n// cfg contains only fields kubectl owns; others are nil/zero\n```\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Operational Implications and Tradeoffs\n\n### 6.1 Performance Implications\n\n#### Managed Fields Storage Overhead\n\n**Impact:** Each resource carries array of `managedFields` entries\n\n**Size per manager:**\n- ~200 bytes for metadata (manager name, timestamp, apiVersion, operation)\n- ~2\u201310x the field paths size (depends on object complexity)\n\n**Example:** ConfigMap with 50 keys\n- One manager entry: ~1\u20132 KB\n- Five managers: ~5\u201310 KB added to resource\n\n**Mitigation:** `capmanagers` implementation limits field managers per resource (line 1\u201350 in capmanagers.go)\n\n```go\n// Caps number of managers if list grows too large\n// Default: keep only 10 most recent managers\n```\n\nOlder managers are automatically pruned to prevent unbounded growth.\n\n#### Storage Write Amplification\n\n**Noop applies** (applying unchanged configuration) still write to etcd:\n- ManagedFields timestamp always updates\n- ResourceVersion increments\n- Triggers all watchers\n\n**Mitigation:**\n- `IgnoreManagedFieldsTimestampsTransformer` skips writes if fields unchanged\n- Environment variable: `KUBE_APISERVER_AVOID_NOOP_SSA_TIMESTAMP_UPDATES=true`\n\n**Recommendation:** Enable for clusters with high apply frequency (GitOps controllers).\n\n#### Conflict Detection Latency\n\n**Scenario:** Apply with many fields, multiple managers own various fields\n\n**Latency:** O(num_managers \u00d7 num_fields_in_patch)\n- Structured merge diff library compares field paths\n- Conflict checking is fast (hash lookups) but expensive at scale\n\n**Typical latency:** <50ms per apply request (on standard hardware)\n\n**Worst case:** Apply touching 1000 fields with 100 managers \u2192 possible 5+ second conflict resolution\n\n**Recommendation:** Limit number of managers per resource via capmanagers tuning.\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Data Correctness\n\n#### Orphaned Managers\n\n**Scenario:** Webhook that managed fields is deleted but its ManagedFieldsEntry remains\n\n**Effect:** Fields appear \"owned\" by non-existent manager; no one can safely modify them\n\n**Detection:** Admin tools can scan for managers not in `--authorization-kubeconfig` or webhook registry\n\n**Resolution:** Manual removal from managedFields or force-apply\n\n**Mitigation:** Admission controller cleanup hooks (not built-in; requires custom controller)\n\n#### Concurrent Apply Races\n\n**Scenario:** Two clients apply simultaneously to the same resource\n\n**Kubernetes handling:**\n1. Both read current object with resourceVersion V1\n2. Both compute merged objects\n3. First write succeeds, updates resourceVersion to V2\n4. Second write fails (resourceVersion mismatch)\n5. Second client is told to retry\n6. GuaranteedUpdate retry loop handles this transparently\n\n**Outcome:** Both applies eventually succeed (ordering depends on retry luck)\n\n**Note:** Not \"last-write-wins\" like traditional updates; both managers' fields are merged.\n\n#### Field Manager Name Stability\n\n**Risk:** If client changes its field manager name (e.g., \"controller-v1\" \u2192 \"controller-v2\"), old entries persist\n\n**Effect:**\n- Original fields still owned by \"controller-v1\"\n- New apply claims fields under \"controller-v2\"\n- ManagedFields now has both entries\n\n**Best practice:** Field manager names should be stable identifiers (namespace/label + component name)\n\n**Example:**\n```\n# Good: includes namespace and component\nfieldManager=kube-system:deployment-controller\n\n# Bad: includes version (changes break ownership tracking)\nfieldManager=deployment-controller-v2.3.1\n```\n\n### 6.3 Debugging and Observability\n\n#### Managed Fields Inspection\n\n**Tool:** `kubectl get resource -o json | jq '.metadata.managedFields'`\n\n**Output example:**\n```json\n[\n  {\n    \"manager\": \"kubectl\",\n    \"operation\": \"Apply\",\n    \"apiVersion\": \"apps/v1\",\n    \"time\": \"2024-02-28T10:30:00Z\",\n    \"fieldsType\": \"FieldsV1\",\n    \"fieldsV1\": {\n      \"f:metadata\": {\"f:labels\": {\"f:app\": {}}},\n      \"f:spec\": {\"f:replicas\": {}}\n    }\n  },\n  {\n    \"manager\": \"flux\",\n    \"operation\": \"Apply\",\n    \"apiVersion\": \"apps/v1\",\n    \"time\": \"2024-02-28T11:00:00Z\",\n    \"fieldsType\": \"FieldsV1\",\n    \"fieldsV1\": {\n      \"f:spec\": {\n        \"f:template\": {\n          \"f:spec\": {\"f:containers\": {}}\n        }\n      }\n    }\n  }\n]\n```\n\n**Interpretation:**\n- kubectl manages labels and replicas count\n- flux manages pod template containers\n- No conflicts (different fields)\n\n#### Conflict Error Messages\n\n**Example from conflict.go:**\n```\nApply failed with 2 conflicts:\n  conflicts with \"kube-controller-manager\" using apps/v1 at 2024-02-28T11:00:00Z:\n    - .spec.replicas\n  conflicts with \"admission-webhook\" using batch/v1:\n    - .spec.template.spec.volumes[0].emptyDir\n```\n\n**What it means:**\n- Two different managers own fields you're trying to apply\n- Manager names include timestamps for debugging which version created the entry\n\n**How to resolve:**\n```bash\n# Option 1: Force-apply (takes ownership of conflicting fields)\nkubectl apply -f patch.yaml --overwrite=true\n\n# Option 2: Coordinate with other manager\n# Contact kube-controller-manager owners to remove their claim\n\n# Option 3: Manual edit (use with extreme caution)\nkubectl edit deployment my-deployment  # Remove manager entries from managedFields\n```\n\n#### Audit Logging\n\n**Trigger:** All patch requests logged by audit subsystem\n\n**Recorded data:**\n- Request method (PATCH)\n- Content-Type (shows patch type)\n- FieldManager name\n- Force flag value\n- Result (success/conflict/validation error)\n- Applied diff (if enabled)\n\n**Configuration:** Via audit policy in API server config\n\n**Use case:** Compliance auditing (\"who applied what when\") and debugging (\"why did this patch fail?\")\n\n### 6.4 Operational Best Practices\n\n#### Naming Field Managers\n\n**Standard pattern:** `namespace/component`\n\nExamples:\n- `argocd/argocd-controller` (Argo CD deployment namespace)\n- `flux-system/flux-helm-controller`\n- `default/manual-operator`\n- `kube-system/kubelet` (built-in)\n\n**Benefit:** Easily identifies which system/namespace manages fields\n\n#### Managing Owner Conflicts in GitOps\n\n**Pattern 1: Single-owner (recommended)**\n- One GitOps controller (Flux, ArgoCD) manages entire resource\n- All other controllers only manage subresources (e.g., `.status`)\n- No conflicts, clean ownership\n\n**Pattern 2: Multi-owner with explicit coordination**\n- Each operator owns specific fields (enforce via policy)\n- Example:\n  - Flux manages `.spec.replicas` (scaling policy)\n  - Metrics-Server manages `.status.conditions` (auto-scaling results)\n  - Webhook manages `.metadata.annotations.injected` (sidecar injection)\n- Requires careful coordination; document in runbook\n\n**Pattern 3: Force-apply + migration**\n- New system force-applies to take ownership from old system\n- Old system is deprecated and shut down\n- Temporary conflicts expected during migration\n- Document in change log\n\n#### Handling Admission Webhook Side Effects\n\n**Scenario:** Webhook mutates objects during apply (e.g., injects sidecar)\n\n**Best practice:**\n1. Webhook uses `force=true` internally if it needs to modify fields\n2. Or webhook only modifies fields no manager owns yet\n3. Or webhook avoids modifying fields during apply (only during update)\n\n**Monitoring:** Watch for warnings in response headers:\n```\nWarning: 299 - \".metadata.managedFields was in an invalid state after admission\"\n```\n\nIf seen frequently, audit the webhook configuration.\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Critical File and Directory Map\n\nThis section maps the most important files and directories used in SSA/apply configuration analysis.\n\n### Client-Side ApplyConfigurations\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/` | Root directory for all generated apply configuration types |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/core/v1/configmap.go` | Example: ConfigMapApplyConfiguration struct and builder methods |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/utils.go` | `ForKind()` dispatcher; maps GroupVersionKind to apply config instance |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/applyconfigurations/internal/` | Internal types shared across all apply configs |\n\n### Code Generation\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/main.go` | Entry point for applyconfiguration-gen tool |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/generators/` | Generator logic; creates apply config source files |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/code-generator/cmd/applyconfiguration-gen/args/` | CLI argument parsing |\n\n### Server-Side Patch Handling\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` | Main patch handler; dispatcher for all patch types (JSON Patch, Merge Patch, SMP, SSA) |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` line 68 | `PatchResource()` handler registration |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/endpoints/handlers/patch.go` line 272 | `patcher` struct; `NewConflictError()` |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/managedfields.go` | ManagedFields entry encoding/decoding |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/capmanagers.go` | Field manager limit enforcement |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/internal/structuredmerge.go` | Structured merge diff coordination with fieldpath library |\n\n### Type Conversion and Parsing\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/managedfields/typeconverter.go` | `TypeConverter` interface; recovers manager's applied config from managedFields |\n\n### Serialization and Encoding\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|------|---------|\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime/serializer/cbor/` | CBOR encoder/decoder (used for apply-patch+cbor) |\n| `/workspace/staging/src/k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/yaml/` | YAML unmarshaler (used for apply-patch+yaml) |\n\n### External Dependencies\n\n| Package | Purpose |\n|---------|---------|\n| `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6` | Structured merge diff algorithm; computes field path conflicts and merging |\n| `sigs.k8s.io/structured-merge-diff/v6/fieldpath` | Field path representation; nested map structure for field ownership |\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Summary and Key Takeaways\n\n### What SSA Solves\n\nServer-Side Apply enables safe, multi-actor field ownership in Kubernetes by:\n\n1. **Tracking ownership**: ManagedFields records which manager owns each field\n2. **Detecting conflicts**: Prevents overwriting fields owned by other managers (unless force-applied)\n3. **Declarative merging**: Clients declare desired state; server merges multiple declarations\n4. **Field-level granularity**: Multiple managers can safely edit different fields of same resource\n\n### Key Components\n\n| Component | Role |\n|-----------|------|\n| **ApplyConfiguration** | Type-safe builders for constructing apply patches (client-side) |\n| **PatchResource handler** | HTTP dispatch for all patch types; selects mechanism |\n| **ApplyPatcher mechanism** | Server-side SSA logic; unmarshals YAML/CBOR, calls FieldManager |\n| **FieldManager** | Core ownership tracking; computes conflicts, merges fields |\n| **ManagedFieldsEntry** | Persistent record of field ownership in resource metadata |\n| **Admission wrapper** | Validates that webhooks don't corrupt managedFields |\n\n### Request Flow Essence\n\n```\nClient PATCH (apply-patch+yaml)\n  \u2192 PatchResource handler\n  \u2192 Select applyPatcher mechanism\n  \u2192 Unmarshal YAML patch\n  \u2192 FieldManager.Apply() [core SSA logic]\n    \u2192 Check field ownership conflicts\n    \u2192 Merge non-conflicting fields\n    \u2192 Update managedFields\n  \u2192 Admission validation\n  \u2192 GuaranteedUpdate storage write\n  \u2192 Return 200 OK with merged object\n```\n\n### Common Operational Patterns\n\n**GitOps + SSA:** Single operator (Flux/Argo) applies entire resource; other components manage subresources only\n\n**Admission webhooks + SSA:** Webhooks mutate; SSA preserves field ownership integrity\n\n**Debugging conflicts:** Check `.metadata.managedFields` to see who owns which fields\n\n**Force-apply:** Use when migrating ownership between systems; document the migration\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nServer-Side Apply represents a fundamental shift from imperative, last-write-wins updates to declarative, coordinated field ownership. By embedding field manager identity and ownership directly in resource metadata, Kubernetes enables multiple control planes, webhooks, and operators to safely coexist.\n\nThe subsystem is deeply integrated across multiple layers: API server request handlers manage the HTTP interface, field manager implementations track ownership, admission plugins validate mutations, and client-side apply configurations provide type-safe builders. Understanding the boundaries and responsibilities of each component is essential for debugging conflicts, designing multi-manager systems, and operating Kubernetes at scale.\n",

# Kubernetes Server-Side Apply Configuration Guide

## Executive Summary

Server-Side Apply (SSA) is a declarative resource management system in Kubernetes that enables safe, concurrent ownership of fields across multiple controllers, tools, and operators. Unlike imperative updates, SSA tracks which client (field manager) owns each field and automatically resolves conflicts when multiple clients attempt to modify the same fields. This guide details the subsystem architecture, component responsibilities, request flow, conflict handling, and operational patterns.

---

## Part 1: Subsystem Purpose and Boundaries

### Purpose

Server-Side Apply solves the multi-actor field ownership problem: In Kubernetes, many clients (human operators, deployment controllers, admission webhooks, operators) need to concurrently modify resources. Without coordination, their changes collide and overwrite each other.

SSA provides:

1. **Field-level ownership tracking** via `managedFields` in resource metadata
2. **Conflict detection** when clients try to modify fields owned by others
3. **Declarative merging** of configurations from multiple managers
4. **Dry-run support** to preview apply operations before committing
5. **Force-apply capability** to override field ownership when necessary

The core philosophy: *Clients declare their desired state; the server merges multiple declarations into a unified object while preserving ownership boundaries.*

### Boundaries and Scope

**In Scope (SSA responsibility):**
- Patch processing for `application/apply-patch+yaml` and `application/apply-patch+cbor` content types
- Structured merge diff using fieldpath-based conflict detection
- Managed fields entry creation and update (in `.metadata.managedFields`)
- Field manager identity tracking and conflic
... (truncated)
